<p><b>Cantabria</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <small>also</small> <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span></span>-/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[kanˈtaβɾja]</a></span>)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Pronunciation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Pronunciation"><span title="Cantabrian IPA transcription needed for this word. You can help!">needs Cantabrian IPA</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous community">autonomous community</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> with <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a> as its capital city. It is recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">historic community</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and is bordered on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Autonomous Community</a> (<a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">province of Biscay</a>), on the south by <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a> (<a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">provinces of León</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palencia_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Palencia (province)">Palencia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Burgos" title="Province of Burgos">Burgos</a>), on the west by the <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Principality of Asturias</a>, and on the north by the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Cantabrian Sea</a> (Bay of Biscay).
</p><p>Cantabria belongs to <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Spain" title="Green Spain">Green Spain</a></i>, the name given to the strip of land between the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cantabrian Mountains</a>, so called because of its particularly lush vegetation, due to the wet and moderate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>. The climate is strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> winds trapped by the mountains; the average annual precipitation is about 1,200&#160;mm (47 inches).
</p><p>Cantabria has archaeological sites from the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> period, although the first signs of human occupation date from the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a>. The most significant site for cave paintings is that in the <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_Altamira" title="Cave of Altamira">cave of Altamira</a>, dating from about 37,000 BC<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and declared, along with nine other Cantabrian caves, as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.
</p><p>The modern Province of Cantabria was constituted on 28 July 1778 at Puente San Miguel, Reocín. The <a href="/wiki/Organic_Law_(Spain)" title="Organic Law (Spain)">Organic Law</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_Statute_of_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomy Statute of Cantabria">Autonomy Statute of Cantabria</a> was approved on 30 December 1981, giving the region its own institutions of self-government.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png/350px-Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png/525px-Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png/700px-Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png 2x" data-file-width="1529" data-file-height="1016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Physical_map_of_Cantabria_-_Spain.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographical map of Cantabria.</div></div></div>
<p>Numerous authors, including <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_Caro_Baroja" title="Julio Caro Baroja">Julio Caro Baroja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aureliano_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Guerra" class="mw-redirect" title="Aureliano Fernández Guerra">Aureliano Fernández Guerra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Schulten" title="Adolf Schulten">Adolf Schulten</a>, have explored the etymology of the name <i>Cantabria</i>, yet its origins remain uncertain. The Online Etymology Dictionary states the root <i>cant-</i> is said to come from the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a> for "rock" or "rocky",<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> while <i>-abr</i> was a common suffix used in Celtic regions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGonzález_Echegaray1993_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGonzález_Echegaray1993-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Thus, <i>Cantabrian</i> could mean "people who live in the rocks" or "<a href="/wiki/Highland_(geography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Highland (geography)">highlanders</a>", a reference to the steep and mountainous territory of Cantabria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGonzález_Echegaray1993_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGonzález_Echegaray1993-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The name <i>Cantabria</i> could also be related to the Celtic root "kant" or "cant" meaning edge or rim thus "coastal district," or "corner-land", "land on the edge" thus having the same probable derivation as the name of the English county  of <i><a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor,_Santander.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor%2C_Santander.jpg/220px-Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor%2C_Santander.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor%2C_Santander.jpg/330px-Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor%2C_Santander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor%2C_Santander.jpg/440px-Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor%2C_Santander.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5395" data-file-height="3597" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Near_the_Faro_de_Cabo_Mayor,_Santander.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cabo Mayor and entrance to the harbor, Santander</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relief">Relief</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Relief">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Cantabria is a mountainous and coastal region, with important natural resources. It has two distinct areas which are well differentiated morphologically:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Coast</b>. A coastal strip of low, wide and gently rolling valleys some 10 kilometres in width, the altitude of which does not rise above 500 metres, and which meets the ocean in a line of abrupt cliffs broken by river estuaries, forming <a href="/wiki/Ria" title="Ria">rias</a> and beaches.  <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander Bay">Santander Bay</a> is the most prominent indentation in the coastline. To the south, the coastal strip rises to meet the mountains.</li>
<li><b>Mountains</b>. This is a long barrier made up of abruptly rising mountains parallel to the sea, which are part of the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cantabrian Mountains</a>. The mountains are mostly made of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> with <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> topography, and occupy most of Cantabria's area. They form deep valleys running north-south. The torrential rivers are short, fast flowing and of great eroding power, so the slopes are steep. The valleys define different natural regions, delimited physically by the intervening mountain ranges: <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A9bana" title="Liébana">Liébana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saja-Nansa" class="mw-redirect" title="Saja-Nansa">Saja-Nansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Besaya_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Besaya valley">Besaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pas_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Pas River">Pas</a>-<a href="/wiki/Pisue%C3%B1a_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Pisueña River">Pisueña</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miera_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Miera valley">Miera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_As%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Valley of Asón">Asón</a>-<a href="/wiki/G%C3%A1ndara" title="Gándara">Gándara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campoo" title="Campoo">Campoo</a>. To the 'mountain' region belongs the <a href="/wiki/Escudo_de_Cabu%C3%A9rniga_Range" class="mw-redirect" title="Escudo de Cabuérniga Range">Escudo Range</a>, a mountain range of 600 to 1,000 metres (2,000 to 3,300&#160;ft) high that covers 15 or 20&#160;km (9.3 or 12.4&#160;mi) in a parallel line to the coast in the West part of Cantabria.</li></ul>
<p>Towards the south are higher mountains, the tops of which form the watershed between the drainage basins of the Rivers <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duero" class="mw-redirect" title="Duero">Duero</a> and the rivers that flow into the Bay of Biscay. These peaks generally exceed 1,500&#160;m (4,900&#160;ft) from the Pass of San Glorio in the west to the Pass of Los Tornos in the eastern part: Peña Labra, <a href="/wiki/Castro_Valnera" title="Castro Valnera">Castro Valnera</a> and the mountain passes of Sejos, El Escudo and La Sía. The great limestone masses of <a href="/wiki/Picos_de_Europa" title="Picos de Europa">Picos de Europa</a> also stand out in the southwest of the region: most of their summits exceed 2,500&#160;m (8,200&#160;ft), and their topography is shaped by the former presence of <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:1002px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg/1000px-Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg/1500px-Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f3/Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1662" data-file-height="275" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panoramica_Alisas_Cantabria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama of the gateway to Alisas, in the <i><a href="/wiki/Municipio" title="Municipio">municipio</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Riotuerto" title="Riotuerto">Riotuerto</a>, Cantabria</div></div></div></div>
<p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_stream" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf stream">gulf stream</a>, Cantabria, as well as the rest of "Green Spain", has a much more <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> climate than might be expected for its latitude, which is comparable to that of <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>. The region has a humid <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, with warm summers and mild winters. Annual <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> is around 1,200&#160;mm at the coasts and higher in the mountains. The mean temperature is about 14&#160;°C (57.2&#160;°F). Snow is frequent in higher zones of Cantabria between the months of October and March. Some zones of Picos de Europa, over 2,500 metres high, have an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine climate</a> with snow persisting year round. The driest months are July and August. The mountainous relief of Cantabria has a dominant effect on local microclimate in Cantabria. It is the main cause of the peculiar meteorologic situations like the so-called "suradas" (<a href="/wiki/%C3%81brego" title="Ábrego">Ábrego</a> wind), due to the <a href="/wiki/Foehn_wind" title="Foehn wind">foehn effect</a>: the southerly wind coming down from the mountains blows strongly and dry, increasing the temperature closer to the coast. This causes a decrease in air humidity and rainfall. These conditions are more frequent in autumn and winter, and the temperatures are commonly higher than 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F). Fires are often helped by this type of wind: one example is the fire that destroyed part of the city of Santander in the winter of 1941. In these specific cases in the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Cant%C3%A1brica" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Cantábrica">mountain range</a> the <a href="/wiki/Lapse_rate" title="Lapse rate">dry adiabatic gradient</a> produces different conditions to the rest of the region: the wind there is fresher and more humid, and there is more rain.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The rivers of Cantabria are short and rapid, descending steeply because the sea is so close to their source in the Cantabrian Mountains. They flow perpendicular to the coastline, except for the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a>. They also generally <a href="/wiki/Discharge_(hydrology)" title="Discharge (hydrology)">flow</a> year round due to constant rainfall. Nevertheless, the rate of flow is modest (20 m³/s annual average) compared to the other rivers of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a>. The rapidness of their waters, caused by their steep descents, gives them great <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosive</a> power, creating the narrow V-shaped valleys characteristic of Green Spain. The environmental condition of the rivers is generally good, although increasing human activity due to rising population in the valleys continues to pose a challenge.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG/220px-Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG/330px-Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG/440px-Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG 2x" data-file-width="860" data-file-height="584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nacimiento_del_rio_Ason_-_Source_of_the_Ason_river.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Source_(river_or_stream)" class="mw-redirect" title="Source (river or stream)">source</a> of the Asón River</div></div></div>
<p>The main rivers of the region, sorted by <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basin</a>, are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_North_Basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Spanish North Basin (page does not exist)">North Basin</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> (flows into the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Sea" title="Cantabrian Sea">Cantabrian Sea</a>)
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ag%C3%BCera_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Agüera River (page does not exist)">Agüera</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/As%C3%B3n_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Asón River">Asón</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Besaya_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Besaya River (page does not exist)">Besaya</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Deva_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Deva River">Deva</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miera_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Miera River (page does not exist)">Miera</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nansa_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nansa River (page does not exist)">Nansa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pas_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Pas River">Pas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saja_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Saja River">Saja</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ebro_Basin" title="Ebro Basin">Ebro Basin</a><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> (flows into the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>)
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=H%C3%ADjar_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Híjar River (page does not exist)">Híjar</a></li>
<li>Ebro</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duero_Basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Duero Basin (page does not exist)">Duero Basin</a><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> (flows into the Atlantic Ocean)</li></ul>
<p>Cantabria is the only autonomous community whose rivers flow into every one of the seas which surround the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>: The Cantabrian Sea, the Atlantic Ocean and the Mediterranean Sea.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vegetation">Vegetation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Vegetation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prau.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Prau.JPG/220px-Prau.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Prau.JPG/330px-Prau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Prau.JPG/440px-Prau.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prau.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grassland in <a href="/wiki/Vald%C3%A1liga" title="Valdáliga">Valdáliga</a></div></div></div>
<p>The variation in the altitude of the region, which in a short distance ranges from sea level to 2,600 meters in the mountains, leads to a great deal of diversity in vegetation and a large number of <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a>.
Cantabria has vegetation typical of the Atlantic side of the Iberian Peninsula. It is characterized by forests of leafy <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">deciduous</a> trees such as oak and <a href="/wiki/European_beech" class="mw-redirect" title="European beech">European beech</a>. Nevertheless, human intervention dating back to ancient times has favored the creation of pastures, allowing the existence of large areas of grassland and prairies suitable for grazing cattle. These grasslands are mingled with plantations of <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> and native oak. The southern part of Cantabria, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a></i> of Campoo the fringes of the Castilian plateau, is characterized by the transition to drier vegetation. Another diversifying factor which contributes to local variation within the region is the Mediterranean <a href="/wiki/Ecotone" title="Ecotone">ecotone</a>, giving rise to species unique to the region, such as the <a href="/wiki/Holm_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Holm oak">holm oak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arbutus" title="Arbutus">arbutus trees</a>, which are found in poor limestone soils with little moisture.
</p><p>In Cantabria there are several zones of plant life:
</p>
<ul><li><b>The coastal strip</b>, including sandy dunes with minimal vegetation. Adjacent to these are steep cliffs with plants unique to that type of terrain.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hills_of_La_Marina_(Cantabria).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Hills_of_La_Marina_%28Cantabria%29.jpg/220px-Hills_of_La_Marina_%28Cantabria%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Hills_of_La_Marina_%28Cantabria%29.jpg/330px-Hills_of_La_Marina_%28Cantabria%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Hills_of_La_Marina_%28Cantabria%29.jpg/440px-Hills_of_La_Marina_%28Cantabria%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hills_of_La_Marina_(Cantabria).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hills and ria typical of a landscape from the maritime region</div></div></div>
<ul><li><b>The maritime region</b>, near the coast and including altitudes up to 500 metres. Originally it had mixed deciduous forests containing <a href="/wiki/Ash_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Ash tree">ash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tilia" title="Tilia">linden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_laurel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay laurel">bay laurel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hazel" title="Hazel">hazel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maple" title="Maple">maple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Populus" title="Populus">poplar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">birch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holm_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Holm oak">holm oak</a>, and others. The <a href="/wiki/Riparian" class="mw-redirect" title="Riparian">riparian</a> parts were filled with forests of <a href="/wiki/Alder" title="Alder">alder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willow" title="Willow">willow</a>. Today these native forests have almost completely disappeared, leaving only reserves in area of poor arability. In their place there are grasslands which are quite productive in the temperate climate and which sustain the economy of rural Cantabria. Next to these are very large <a href="/wiki/Monoculture" title="Monoculture">monoculture</a> plantations of <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> for paper production, of disastrous ecological consequences to the biodiversity and climate of the region.</li></ul><p>
During the last two decades of the 20th century, and due mainly to European agricultural policies (<a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">CAP</a>), many farmers were forced to substitute forestry for livestock farming, so as to avoid unemployment and poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup> This provoked a surge of <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> - <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eucalyptus#Reforestación_mediante_eucaliptos_en_España" class="extiw" title="es:Eucalyptus">see eucalyptus article on Spanish Wikipedia</a> - plantations (and to a less extent of <a href="/wiki/Pinus_radiata" title="Pinus radiata">pines</a>) which often hid the illegal destruction of native forests, just as the spread of livestock farming had done in the past by the endemic conversion of forest into prairie. These acts have been laxly controlled by the local councils or the central governments, in a process that clearly follows the saying: "<i>Pan para hoy, hambre para mañana</i>" (which translates as: "short-term gain, long-term pain").</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg/300px-Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="71" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg/450px-Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg/600px-Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2103" data-file-height="497" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Relieve_karstico-Karst_topography.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama of the Cantabrian Mountains to the left and the port city of Santander in the distant right. The peak <i>Alto de Brenas</i> in <a href="/wiki/Riotuerto" title="Riotuerto">Riotuerto</a> has a height of 579 metres.</div></div></div><p>The plantation of pines has given way in the last decades to that of eucalyptus due to the fact this <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">non-indigenous species</a> has no natural attacker within the European ecosystem (while pines are highly vulnerable to the <a href="/wiki/Pine_processionary" title="Pine processionary">pine processionary</a>).
</p><p>Both in relative and absolute terms the use of woods for forestry has increased in Cantabria, and is now almost 70% of all woods in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>The foothills</b>, from 500 to 1,100 metres altitude are colonized by monoculture forests of oak (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_robur" title="Quercus robur">Quercus robur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_petraea" title="Quercus petraea">Quercus petraea</a></i>) on the sunnier slopes. In more shaded areas and especially from about 800 metres there are forests of <a href="/wiki/European_beech" class="mw-redirect" title="European beech">European beech</a> which are the main food source in winter for many animal species.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pico_Tordias.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Pico_Tordias.jpg/300px-Pico_Tordias.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Pico_Tordias.jpg/450px-Pico_Tordias.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Pico_Tordias.jpg/600px-Pico_Tordias.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2139" data-file-height="608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pico_Tordias.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Brañas</i>, or mountain <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">prairies</a> in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Arenas_de_Igu%C3%B1a" title="Arenas de Iguña">Arenas de Iguña</a>. In the distance, the Picos de Europa can be seen. Tordías Peak is 968 metres high.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The <b>subalpine plane</b>, in this high country, the plant life is composed of birch, scrub, and <a href="/wiki/Poaceae" title="Poaceae">grasses</a> which are especially important for the economy because during the summer they serve as pasture for grazing cattle and horses.</li></ul>
<p>Along with these characteristics it would also be necessary to mention peculiarities of the <i>comarca</i> of <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A9bana" title="Liébana">Liébana</a>, which has a <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimate</a> very similar to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a>, allowing to grow <a href="/wiki/Cork_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Cork oak">cork oaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vine" title="Vine">vines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, and which is still very well conserved from human activity.
The other remarkable <i>comarca</i> is <a href="/wiki/Campoo" title="Campoo">Campoo</a>, in southern Cantabria, with its Pyrenean oak.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_parks">Natural parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Natural parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png/220px-Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png/330px-Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png/440px-Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png 2x" data-file-width="1167" data-file-height="734" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parques_Naturales_y_Nacionales_de_Cantabria.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Natural_park_(Spain)" title="Natural park (Spain)">Natural</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a> in Cantabria</div></div></div>
<p>There are seven natural areas in this autonomous community designated as <a href="/wiki/Natural_park_(Spain)" title="Natural park (Spain)">Natural</a> or <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Picos_de_Europa_National_Park" title="Picos de Europa National Park">Picos de Europa</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="National Park">National Park</a></li>
<li>Collados del Asón Natural Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Santo%C3%B1a,_Victoria_and_Joyel_Marshes_Natural_Park" title="Santoña, Victoria and Joyel Marshes Natural Park">Santoña, Victoria and Joyel Marshes Natural Park</a></li>
<li>Macizo de Peña Cabarga Natural Park</li>
<li>Oyambre Natural Park</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saja-Besaya_Natural_Park" title="Saja-Besaya Natural Park">Saja-Besaya Natural Park</a></li>
<li>Dunes of Liencres Natural Park</li></ul>
<p>The most important of these is the Picos de Europa National Park, which affects Castile and León and Asturias in addition to Cantabria, the three autonomous communities sharing its management.
Santoña, Victoria and Joyel <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marshes</a> are also <a href="/wiki/Special_Protection_Area" title="Special Protection Area">Special Protection Areas</a> for the birds (ZEPA<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>).
</p><p>Furthermore, nine <a href="/wiki/Site_of_Community_Importance" title="Site of Community Importance">Sites of Community Importance</a> (LIC<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>) have been declared: Western Mountain, Eastern Mountain, Western Rias and Oyambre Dunes, Dunes of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Liencres&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Liencres (page does not exist)">Liencres</a> and Estuary of the Pas, El Puntal Dunes and Estuary of the Miera, Ria de Ajo, Marshes of <a href="/wiki/Noja" title="Noja">Noja</a>-<a href="/wiki/Santo%C3%B1a" title="Santoña">Santoña</a>, <a href="/wiki/Escudo_de_Cabu%C3%A9rniga_Range" class="mw-redirect" title="Escudo de Cabuérniga Range">Escudo de Cabuérniga Range</a> and several caves with important <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bat</a> colonies.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="text-align:right;padding:1px">467,138</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+8.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1981</th><td style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2011</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">592,542</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+10.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2017</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">581,477</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−1.9%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px
