<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png/200px-Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png/300px-Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png/400px-Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png 2x" data-file-width="812" data-file-height="594" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Piramid_Population_Cantabria_2006.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">Population pyramid</a> for Cantabria for 2006 from the municipal planning authority.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png/200px-Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png/300px-Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png/400px-Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png 2x" data-file-width="936" data-file-height="662" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_population_of_Cantabria_2005.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Demographic map showing centres of population in 2005.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the 2009 census, the region has a population of 591,886<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> which constitutes 1.29% of the population of Spain, with the population density numbering 106.8 people per kilometer. The average life expectancy for male inhabitants is 75 years; for female inhabitants, it is 83 years. Eight years later in 2017 the population has fallen to 581,477 according to INE.
</p><p>In relative contrast to other regions of Spain, Cantabria has not experienced much immigration. In 2007, only 4.7% of the population were immigrants. The predominant countries of origin for immigrants to Cantabria are <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of the population resides in the coastal area, particularly in two cities: <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a>, with 183,000 people, and <a href="/wiki/Torrelavega" title="Torrelavega">Torrelavega</a>, the second largest urban and industrial centre in Cantabria, having a population of around 60,000. These two cities form a <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> known as the Santander-Torrelavega metropolitan area. <a href="/wiki/Castro_Urdiales" title="Castro Urdiales">Castro Urdiales</a> has an official population of 28,542,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> making it the fourth largest in the region because of its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> metropolitan area, there are a large number of people not registered in Castro Urdiales, and the true count may be double the official figure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The most important municipalities of Cantabria are the following:
</p>
<ol><li><b><a href="/wiki/Santander,_Spain" title="Santander, Spain">Santander</a></b> (pop. 184,661)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Torrelavega" title="Torrelavega">Torrelavega</a></b> (pop. 55,947)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Camargo,_Cantabria" title="Camargo, Cantabria">Camargo</a></b> (pop. 32,000)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Castro-Urdiales" class="mw-redirect" title="Castro-Urdiales">Castro-Urdiales</a></b> (pop. 31.670)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Pi%C3%A9lagos" title="Piélagos">Piélagos</a></b> (pop. 20,081)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/El_Astillero" title="El Astillero">El Astillero</a></b> (pop. 17,360)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Laredo,_Cantabria" title="Laredo, Cantabria">Laredo</a></b> (pop. 12,591)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Los_Corrales_de_Buelna" title="Los Corrales de Buelna">Los Corrales de Buelna</a></b> (pop. 11,610)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Bezana" title="Santa Cruz de Bezana">Santa Cruz de Bezana</a></b> (pop. 11,279)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Santo%C3%B1a" title="Santoña">Santoña</a></b> (pop. 11,569)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Reinosa" title="Reinosa">Reinosa</a></b> (pop. 10,307)</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Empire">Roman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Roman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Tarraconensis" title="Hispania Tarraconensis">Hispania Tarraconensis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantabri" title="Cantabri">Cantabri</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberia_300BC-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Iberia_300BC-en.svg/200px-Iberia_300BC-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Iberia_300BC-en.svg/300px-Iberia_300BC-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Iberia_300BC-en.svg/400px-Iberia_300BC-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="924" data-file-height="762" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberia_300BC-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Language groups of <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_Peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Roman Peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman Iberia</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cantabria_prerromana.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Cantabria_prerromana.svg/200px-Cantabria_prerromana.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Cantabria_prerromana.svg/300px-Cantabria_prerromana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Cantabria_prerromana.svg/400px-Cantabria_prerromana.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="992" data-file-height="694" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cantabria_prerromana.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cantabria during the Cantabrian Wars. This map shows the borders of the Cantabrian territory relative to modern Cantabria as well as the different tribes who inhabited it, the neighboring towns, and geographic features with their Latin names.</div></div></div><p>
The first written reference to the name Cantabria emerges around 195 BC, in which the historian <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Elder" title="Cato the Elder">Cato the Elder</a> speaks in his book <i><a href="/wiki/Origines" title="Origines">Origines</a></i> about the source of the Ebro River in the country of the <a href="/wiki/Cantabri" title="Cantabri">Cantabri</a>:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>...The Ebro River starts in the land of the <a href="/wiki/Cantabri" title="Cantabri">Cantabri</a>, large and beautiful, with abundant fish...</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Cato the Elder, <i>Origines: VII</i><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;n 2&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>There are about 150 references to Cantabria or the Cantabri in surviving <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> texts. The Cantabri were used as <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenaries</a> in various conflicts, both within the Iberian Peninsula and elsewhere. It is certain that they participated the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>, from references by <a href="/wiki/Silius_Italicus" title="Silius Italicus">Silius Italicus</a><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Horace" title="Horace">Horace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Hostilius_Mancinus" title="Gaius Hostilius Mancinus">C. Hostilius Mancinus</a> was besieging <a href="/wiki/Numantia" title="Numantia">Numantia</a>, he withdrew upon learning that Cantabri and <a href="/wiki/Vaccaei" title="Vaccaei">Vaccaei</a> were present among his <a href="/wiki/Roman_auxiliaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman auxiliaries">auxiliaries</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Wars" title="Cantabrian Wars">Cantabrian Wars</a> began in <span class="nowrap">29 BC.</span><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> They were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Vipsanius_Agrippa" title="Marcus Vipsanius Agrippa">Agrippa</a> with great slaughter in <span class="nowrap">19 BC</span>, but they revolted again under <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a> and were never entirely subdued.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1878_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1878-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In older geographers, the term Cantabria referred to an expansive country bounded by the Cantabrian Sea (the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>), the western side of the <a href="/wiki/Sella_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Sella River">Sella valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hillfort" title="Hillfort">hillfort</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pe%C3%B1a_Amaya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peña Amaya (page does not exist)">Peña Amaya</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burgos_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgos (province)">Burgos</a>, and along the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguera_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aguera River (page does not exist)">Aguera River</a> almost as far as <a href="/wiki/Castro_Urdiales" title="Castro Urdiales">Castro Urdiales</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It thus included areas of <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Spain" title="Santander, Spain">Santander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">Biscay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guipuzcoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Guipuzcoa">Guipuzcoa</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman conquest of Spain">conquest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Spain</a>, however, it was restricted to the area of <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Spain" title="Santander, Spain">Santander</a> and eastern <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a>, forming a part of <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Tarraconensis" title="Hispania Tarraconensis">Hispania Tarraconensis</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Tarragona" title="Tarragona">Tarragonan</a> Spain").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1878_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1878-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The principal tribes of the area were the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pleutauri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pleutauri (page does not exist)">Pleutauri</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Varduli" title="Varduli">Varduli</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Autrigones" title="Autrigones">Autrigones</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tuisi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tuisi (page does not exist)">Tuisi</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Conisci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Conisci (page does not exist)">Conisci</a> or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concaui&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Concaui (page does not exist)">Concaui</a>, who were known for <a href="/wiki/Blood_drinking" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood drinking">feeding on their horses' blood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;n 3&#93;</a></sup> The area was well settled, with the largest city being <a href="/wiki/Juliobriga" title="Juliobriga">Juliobriga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1878_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1878-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and the local mountains exploited for <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a> mines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1911_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;EB&#39;&#39;1911-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ducado_de_Cantabria.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ducado_de_Cantabria.png/200px-Ducado_de_Cantabria.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ducado_de_Cantabria.png/300px-Ducado_de_Cantabria.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Ducado_de_Cantabria.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ducado_de_Cantabria.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Borders of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cantabria" title="Duchy of Cantabria">Duchy of Cantabria</a></div></div></div>
<p>Following the collapse of the Roman Empire, Cantabria regained its independence from the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>. In 574, King <a href="/wiki/Liuvigild" title="Liuvigild">Liuvigild</a> attacked Cantabria and managed to capture the south of the country, including the city of <a href="/wiki/Amaya_(Burgos)" title="Amaya (Burgos)">Amaya</a>, where he established a Visigothic province called the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cantabria" title="Duchy of Cantabria">Duchy of Cantabria</a> (see picture), which would serve as a <a href="/wiki/Limes" title="Limes">limes</a> or frontier zone to contain the Cantabri as well as their neighbors the <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a>. To the north of this cordon, however, the Cantabri continued to live independently until the Arab invasion. In 714, a mixed <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a>/<a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber</a> army of <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> Moors invaded the upper valleys of the Ebro and succeeded in capturing Amaya, the Cantabrian capital, forcing the Cantabrians back to their traditional frontiers, where they joined forces with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a>.
In the first chronicles of the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a>, Cantabria still appears to be acknowledged as a region. In the <i>Albendense Chronicle</i>, when speaking of <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_I_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso I of Asturias">Alfonso I</a>, it says, "This was the son of <a href="/wiki/Peter_of_Cantabria" title="Peter of Cantabria">Peter</a>, the duke of Cantabria".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;n 4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 9th century, on mentioning the monastery of Saint Zacharias, Eulogius pinpoints it in <i>Seburim</i> (maybe Zubiri) on the river Arga, "waters all of Cantabria", in a letter sent to the bishop of Pamplona Williesind, suggesting a region stretching out far into the east. From this period on, source documents barely reference Cantabria by name, with <i>Asturias</i> featuring in names of the <i>comarcas</i> called <i><a href="/wiki/Asturias_de_Santillana" title="Asturias de Santillana">Asturias de Santillana</a></i>, <i>Asturias de Trasmiera</i> and <i>Asturias de Laredo</i>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg/200px-Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg/300px-Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg/400px-Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2014" data-file-height="1907" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bataille_de_la_Rochelle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Rochelle" title="Battle of La Rochelle">Battle of La Rochelle</a>. Castilian army, formed by Cantabrians from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brotherhood_of_the_Four_Cities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brotherhood of the Four Cities (page does not exist)">Brotherhood of the Four Cities</a>, defeated the English army, getting the control of the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>From a central core formed by the <i>Hermandad de las Cuatro Villas</i> (<i>Brotherhood of the Four Cities</i>) (Santander, Laredo, Castro Urdiales and <a href="/wiki/San_Vicente_de_la_Barquera" title="San Vicente de la Barquera">San Vicente de la Barquera</a>), the <i>Hermandad de las Marismas</i> (<i>Brotherhood of the Marshes</i>) was created, thereby uniting all the important seaports to the East of Asturias. During the period of the Reconquista, the Four Cities actively participated in the re-settling of Andalusia, dispatching men and ships. The coastal port cities of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Puerto_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa" title="El Puerto de Santa María">El Puerto de Santa María</a> were settled by families from the Cantabrian Sea ports. Ships from the Four Cities took part in the taking of <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, destroying the ship bridge linking <a href="/wiki/Triana_(Seville)" class="mw-redirect" title="Triana (Seville)">Triana</a> and Sevilla, a victory that is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">Carrack</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Torre_del_Oro" title="Torre del Oro">Torre del Oro</a> of Sevilla in the coat of arms of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coat_of_arms_of_Santander&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coat of arms of Santander (page does not exist)">Santander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Cantabria" title="Coat of arms of Cantabria">Coat of arms of Cantabria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avil%C3%A9s" title="Avilés">Avilés</a> (Asturias).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_to_18th_centuries">16th to 18th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 16th to 18th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In the 16th century, the name <i>La Montaña</i> (<i>The Mountain</i>) was widespread in popular usage and in literature, as a designation of the Ancient Cantabria, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">Castile</a>, which referred solely to the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Spain#The_Inner_Plateau_and_associated_mountains" title="Geography of Spain">Central Plateau</a>. This distinction has survived into modern times.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg/200px-Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg/300px-Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg/400px-Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="938" data-file-height="1119" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hermandad_de_las_Cuatro_Villas.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brotherhood_of_the_Four_Cities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brotherhood of the Four Cities (page does not exist)">Brotherhood of the Four Cities</a>, antecedent to the Cantabrian region and the main Castilian port at the time.</div></div></div>
<p>With the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>, the Brethren of the Marshes disappeared, leaving the Coregiment of the Four Villas, which included the whole area of influence of the old Brethren of the Four Villas (almost all of Cantabria). During the <i><a href="/wiki/Ancien_R%C3%A9gime" title="Ancien Régime">Ancien Régime</a></i>, the greatest jurisdictional lordships of Cantabria were mainly under the control of three of the <a href="/wiki/Grandee" title="Grandee">Grandee families</a> of Spain: that of <b>Mendoza</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dukedom_of_Infantado" class="mw-redirect" title="Dukedom of Infantado">Dukes of Infantado</a>, Marquises of Santillana), of <b>Manrique de Lara</b> (Marquises of Aguilar de Campoo, Counts of Castañeda), and to a lesser extent that of <b>Velasco</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dukedom_of_Fr%C3%ADas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dukedom of Frías">Dukes of Frías</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constable_of_Castile" title="Constable of Castile">Constables of Castile</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>From the 16th century on, there was renewed interest in studying Cantabria and the Cantabri, particularly concerning the precise location of the territory that this people had occupied. It was not until the 18th century that the debate about the location and size of Ancient Cantabria was settled in a series of works which described the history of the history of the region such as <i>La Cantabria</i><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> by the Augustinian father and historian Enrique Flórez de Setién. Concurrent with the resurgence of this interest in the Cantabrians and the clarification of the aforementioned polemic, many institutions, organizations and jurisdictions in the mountainous territory received the name of "Cantabrian" or "of Cantabria".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1727, the first attempt to unify what would later become the Province of Cantabria occurred. Despite this, the high level of autonomy that the small entities of the fractured estate of Cantabria enjoyed, combined with a lack of resources, continued to be the main reason for Cantabria's weakness, aggravated by the progressive advance of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbonic</a> <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">centralism</a> and its administrative efficiency. The latter continually emphasised the impossibility of the smaller territories facing a multitude of problems on their own: from communications to the exercise of justice, from putting aside adequate reserves for hard times to the indiscriminate <a href="/wiki/Lev%C3%A9e_en_masse" title="Levée en masse">levees</a> for soldiers, and above all the progression of fiscal impositions. All of this led to an acceleration of contact between villas, valleys and jurisdictions, which tended to focus on the Assemblies of the Provinces of the Nine Valleys, led by the deputies elected by the traditional entities of self-government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There were two events that triggered the culmination of the integration process in this second attempt:
</p>
<ul><li>On the one hand, the collective interest in avoiding making contributions to the reconstruction of the bridge of <a href="/wiki/Miranda_de_Ebro" title="Miranda de Ebro">Miranda de Ebro</a>, imposed by order of the Intendant of <a href="/wiki/Burgos" title="Burgos">Burgos</a> on 11 July 1775, the same year that Cantabria suffered two tremendous floods, on 20 June and on 3 November. There was a need to face as the banditry that operated with impunity in Cantabria as a result of a lack of local juridical resources. After the General Deputy of Nine Valleys gathered the affected jurisdictions to the assembly that was to take place in Puente San Miguel on 21 March 1777, they sent their respective deputies with sufficient authority to join with the Nine Valleys.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<p>In this General Assembly a framework was established and formal steps began to be taken, leading to administrative and legal unity in 1778. This all culminated in the success of the Assembly held in the Assembly House of <i>Puente San Miguel</i> on July 28, 1778, where the Province of Cantabria was constituted. It was achieved by passing the common ordinances which had been developed to that end, and which had been discussed and approved previously in councils of all the villas, valleys and subscribed jurisdictions. They were, in addition to the Nine Valleys: Rivadedeva, Peñamellera, the Province of Liébana, Peñarrubia, Lamasón, Rionansa, the Villa of San Vicente de la Barquera, Coto de Estrada, Valdáliga, the Villa of Santillana del Mar, Lugar de Viérnoles, the Villa of Cartes and environs, the Valley of Buelna, the Valley of Cieza, the Valley of Iguña with the Villas of San Vicente and Los Llares, the Villa of Pujayo, the Villa of Pie de Concha y Bárcena, the Valley of Anievas, and the Valley of Toranzo.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnt-baston.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Cnt-baston.PNG/200px-Cnt-baston.PNG" decoding="async" width="200" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Cnt-baston.PNG/300px-Cnt-baston.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Cnt-baston.PNG/400px-Cnt-baston.PNG 2x" data-file-width="905" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnt-baston.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FA8072; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Party and Baton of <a href="/wiki/Laredo,_Cantabria" title="Laredo, Cantabria">Laredo</a> (Province of Cantabria)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #90EE90; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Merindad" title="Merindad">Merindad</a> of <a href="/wiki/Campoo" title="Campoo">Campoo</a> (Province of Toro).</div></div></div></div>
<p>Having learned lessons from the failed attempt of 1727, the first objective of the new entity was to obtain approval from King <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III</a> for the union of all the Cantabrian jurisdictions into one province. The royal ratification was granted on 22 November 1779.
</p><p>The 28 jurisdictions that initially comprised the Province of Cantabria were clear in their intention that all the other jurisdictions that formed the <i>Party and Baton of the Four Villas of the Coast</i> should be included in the new province. To this end they set out the steps needed for this to happen as soon as those jurisdictions should request it. They would have to abide by the ordinances, having the same rights and duties as the founders, all on an equal footing. Thus, the following joined in quick succession: the Abbey of <a href="/wiki/Santillana_del_Mar" title="Santillana del Mar">Santillana</a>, the Valleys of <a href="/wiki/Tudanca" title="Tudanca">Tudanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polaciones" title="Polaciones">Polaciones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herrer%C3%ADas" title="Herrerías">Herrerías</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casta%C3%B1eda" title="Castañeda">Castañeda</a>, the Villa of <a href="/wiki/Torrelavega" title="Torrelavega">Torrelavega</a> and environs, <a href="/wiki/Val_de_San_Vicente" title="Val de San Vicente">Val de San Vicente</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valle_de_Carriedo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Valle de Carriedo (page does not exist)">Valle de Carriedo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tresviso" title="Tresviso">Tresviso</a>, and the Pasiegan Villas of <a href="/w/index.php?title=La_Vega,_Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="La Vega, Cantabria (page does not exist)">La Vega</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Roque,_Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Roque, Cantabria (page does not exist)">San Roque</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Pedro,_Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Pedro, Cantabria (page does not exist)">San Pedro</a>, as well as the city of Santander with its abbey.
</p><p>Competition between the townships of Laredo and Santander led to the latter, having initially allowed the name of Cantabria for the province created at the beginning of the 19th century, later retracting its consent and demanding that it bear the name of Santander, so there would be no doubt as to which was the capital. When in 1821 the Provincial Council presented before the constitutional <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Courts</a> its definitive plan for the provincial borders and legal entities, it proposed the name of Province of Cantabria, to which the Township of Santander replied that "<i>this province must retain the name of Santander</i>". However, many newspapers still showed in their headings the name of Cantabria, or Cantabrian.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg/200px-Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg/300px-Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg/400px-Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estatua_de_Pedro_Velarde_-_Santander.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A statue in Santander erected in honor of Cantabrian artillery captain <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Velarde_y_Santill%C3%A1n" title="Pedro Velarde y Santillán">Pedro Velarde y Santillán</a>, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Spanish war of independence</a>, who died 2 May 1808, during the uprising against the French occupation of Madrid.</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">War of Independence</a> (1808–1814), Bishop Rafael Tomás Menéndez de Luarca, a strong defender of absolutism, promoted himself as the "Regent of Cantabria" and established the <i>Cantabrian Armaments</i> in Santander, a section of the army whose purpose was to travel to all the mountain passes from the Central Plateau to detain any French troop.
</p><p>Although defeated, he managed later to regroup in Liébana under the command of General Juan Díaz Porlier, calling his forces the <i>Cantabrian Division</i>, in which there were various regiments and battalions, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Hussar" title="Hussar">Hussars</a> of Cantabria</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a>) or the <i>Shooters of Cantabria</i> (<a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a>). During the <a href="/wiki/First_Carlist_War" title="First Carlist War">Carlist wars</a> they formed a unit called the <i>Cantabrian Brigade</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The use of terms with ancestral resonance through the 18th and 19th centuries continued during the 20th century, taking on a political tone that was distinctly regionalist, until 1936. In fact, the <i>Republican Federal Party</i> produced an autonomy statute for a Cantabrian-Castilian Federal State that year, which would include present-day Cantabria and any neighbouring areas from <a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> willing to join it. It could not be passed because of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Civil War</a>. Following the war and the subsequent marginalization of such efforts under the <a href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain under Franco">Francoists regime</a>, the use of the name of Cantabria decreased, to the point that for official purposes it was relegated to sports associations, the only arena in which Cantabria was noted as a region. Like other northern regions of Spain, it is less well known to foreign visitors.
</p><p>In 1963, the president of the Provincial Council, Pedro Escalante y Huidobro, proposed reapplying the name of Cantabria to the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Santander" class="mw-redirect" title="Province of Santander">Province of Santander</a>, as suggested in an academic report written by the historian Tomás Maza Solano. Although further steps were taken and many of the townships were in favour of the move, the petition did not succeed, mostly due to the opposition of Santander City Council. On 30 December 1981, a process that had been started in April 1979 by the Council of <a href="/wiki/Cabez%C3%B3n_de_la_Sal" title="Cabezón de la Sal">Cabezón de la Sal</a>, under the presidency of Ambrosio Calzada Hernández, culminated in the granting of self-rule to Cantabria,  outlined in Article 143 of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Constitution">Spanish Constitution</a>.
Cantabria based its claim to autonomy on the constitutional precept that made provision for self-government for "<i>provinces with a historic regional character</i>".
</p><p>A Mixed Assembly formed out of provincial deputies and national members of parliament began the task of drawing up an <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy_of_Cantabria" title="Statute of Autonomy of Cantabria">Autonomy Statute</a> on 10 September 1979. Following the approval of the General Courts on 15 December 1981, the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Carlos I">King of Spain</a> signed the corresponding Organic Law of Autonomy Statute for Cantabria on December 30 of the same year. Thus, the province of Santander broke its link to Castile, and left the former region of Castile and León to which it had belonged up to that time, together with the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_%C3%81vila" title="Province of Ávila">Ávila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Burgos" title="Province of Burgos">Burgos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">León</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Rioja_(Spain)" title="La Rioja (Spain)">Logroño</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Palencia" title="Province of Palencia">Palencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Salamanca" title="Province of Salamanca">Salamanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Segovia" title="Province of Segovia">Segovia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Soria" title="Province of Soria">Soria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Valladolid" title="Province of Valladolid">Valladolid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">Zamora</a>.
</p><p>On 20 February 1982, the first Regional Assembly (now Parliament) was formed, with provisional status. From this time, the former province of Santander has been known as Cantabria and has thereby regained its historic name. The first home-rule elections were held in May 1983. The 4th Legislature (1995–1999) brought into effect the first great reform of the Autonomy Statute of Cantabria, approved by all the parliamentary groups.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_administration">Government and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_Statute_of_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomy Statute of Cantabria">Autonomy Statute of Cantabria</a><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> of 30 December 1981, established that Cantabria has in its institutions the desire to respect fundamental rights and public freedom, at the same time as consolidating and stimulating regional development through democratic channels. This document gathers all competences of the Autonomous Community that were transferred from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Spain" title="Government of Spain">Government of Spain</a>. As in other Autonomous Communities, some competences were not transferred, for example, Justice. The Statute also defines the symbols that should represent the region: The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Cantabria" title="Flag of Cantabria">flag</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Cantabria" title="Coat of arms of Cantabria">coat of arms</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Himno_de_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Himno de Cantabria">anthem of Cantabria</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Cantabria" title="Parliament of Cantabria">Parliament of Cantabria</a><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> is the principal self-government institution of the Autonomous Community, being the representative body of the Cantabrians. Presently it is constituted by thirty-nine deputies elected by universal, equal, free, direct and secret suffrage. The primary functions of the Parliament are: to exercise the <a href="/wiki/Legislation" title="Legislation">legislative power</a>, to approve the budgets of the Autonomous Community, to motivate and control the actions of the government, and to develop the rest of the competences that the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Constitution">Spanish Constitution</a>, the Autonomy Statute and the rest of the legal order bestow on it. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Cantabria" title="President of Cantabria">President of the Autonomous Community</a> holds the highest representation of the Community and ordinary representation of the Country in Cantabria, and presides over the Government, coordinating its activities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Cantabria" title="Government of Cantabria">Government of Cantabria</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> is the body in charge of directing the political activities and exercising the executive and regulatory powers according to the Constitution, the Statute and the laws. The Government is made up of the President, the Vicepresident (in which the President can delegate his executive functions and representations) and the Councillors, who are appointed and ceased by the President.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>After several legislatures presided by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">Partido Popular</a> or by Juan Hormaechea's UPCA, the Regional Government of Cantabria was directed by a coalition of the <a href="/wiki/Regionalist_Party_of_Cantabria" title="Regionalist Party of Cantabria">Regionalist Party of Cantabria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a> (PSOE) from year 2003 until 2011. The President was <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Revilla" title="Miguel Ángel Revilla">Miguel Ángel Revilla</a> of <a href="/wiki/Partido_Regionalista_de_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Partido Regionalista de Cantabria">Partido Regionalista de Cantabria</a> (PRC), and the Vice President was Dolores Gorostiaga of the PSOE. As a result of the absolute majority of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">Partido Popular</a> in the regional elections of 2011, the president from 2011 to 2015 was <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Diego_Palacios" class="mw-redirect" title="Ignacio Diego Palacios">Ignacio Diego Palacios</a>, and the Vice President was also the healthcare Councillor, Maria José Sáenz de Buruaga. After the 2015 regional elections, Miguel Ángel Revilla of Partido Regionalista de Cantabria (PRC) was invested president for a third tenure with the support of PSOE.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_organization">Territorial organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Territorial organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The autonomous community of Cantabria is structured in <i><a href="/wiki/Municipio" title="Municipio">municipios</a></i> (municipalities) and <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarcas</a></i> (regions).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg/400px-Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg/600px-Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg/800px-Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comarcas_administrativas_de_Cantabria.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the municipalities and <i>comarcas</i> of Cantabria <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #AA0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A9bana" title="Liébana">Liébana</a>.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block;
