width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #66FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Trasmiera" title="Trasmiera">Trasmiera</a>.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Valles_Pasiegos" title="Valles Pasiegos">Valles Pasiegos</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<p>There are 102 municipalities in Cantabria generally comprising several townships, and from these, several districts. A number of municipalities bear the name of one of their townships (be it its capital or not), but not all them do. Each municipality is governed by its own <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city</a> or <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council" title="Municipal council">municipal council</a>, and two of them, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tresviso,_Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tresviso, Cantabria (page does not exist)">Tresviso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pesquera,_Cantabria" title="Pesquera, Cantabria">Pesquera</a>, do it by <i>concejo abierto</i> (<i>open council</i>), having fewer than 250 inhabitants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Mancomunidad Campoo-Cabuérniga is not a municipality, but a communal property, singular for its size and characteristics, of shared management between the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Hermandad_de_Campoo_de_Suso" title="Hermandad de Campoo de Suso">Hermandad de Campoo de Suso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabu%C3%A9rniga" title="Cabuérniga">Cabuérniga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Tojos" title="Los Tojos">Los Tojos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruente" title="Ruente">Ruente</a>. This mountain estate is used as a grazing ground for <a href="/wiki/Tudanca_cattle" title="Tudanca cattle">Tudanca cattle</a> and also for horses in less amount, in its <i>brañas</i> or grass prairies, and even nowadays <a href="/wiki/Transhumant" class="mw-redirect" title="Transhumant">transhumant</a> cattle farming traditions survive in this region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>See also:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Cantabria" title="List of municipalities in Cantabria">List of municipalities in Cantabria</a></li></ul>
<h3><span id="Comarcas_.28regions.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Comarcas_(regions)"><i>Comarcas</i> (regions)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Comarcas (regions)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Cantabrian legislation divides the autonomous community in administrative regions called <i>comarcas</i>, but traditionally, other subdivisions of the territory have been used.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Administrative regions</b></li></ul>
<p><i>Law 8/1999 of </i>Comarcas<i> of the Autonomous Community of Cantabria</i> of 28 April 1999 establishes that the comarca is a necessary entity, integral in the territorial organization of the region. This law opens the development of the <i>comarcalization</i> in Cantabria promoting the creation of <i>comarcal</i> entities, which have barely begun to appear. The law establishes that the creation of comarcas will not become mandatory for the whole territory until at least the 70% of it had not been <i>comarcalized</i> by its own will.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="confusing (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It also adds that Santander will not ruled by comarcalization and should establish its own <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> instead.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><i>Comarcas</i> in Cantabria have not reached administrative nature and barely have definite borders. Only Liébana for its geographic position in Picos de Europa, Trasmiera and Campoo, in the Ebro basin are established are clearly defined <i>comarcas</i> in the region. Nevertheless, functional differences in the territory can be distinguished, dividing it in the following areas: <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander Bay">Santander Bay</a>, of industrial and urban nature; <a href="/wiki/Besaya_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Besaya valley">Besaya</a>, also industrial; <a href="/wiki/Saja_and_Nansa_valleys" title="Saja and Nansa valleys">Saja-Nansa</a>, eminently rural; <a href="/wiki/Western_coast_of_Cantabria" title="Western coast of Cantabria">Western Coast</a>, which has urban character; <a href="/wiki/Eastern_coast_of_Cantabria" title="Eastern coast of Cantabria">Eastern Coast</a>, vacational; the traditionally renowned <a href="/wiki/Trasmiera" title="Trasmiera">Trasmiera</a>; rural <a href="/wiki/Valles_Pasiegos" title="Valles Pasiegos">Pas-Miera</a>; <a href="/wiki/As%C3%B3n_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Asón valley">Asón-Agüera</a>, also mainly rural; the very well defined <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A9bana" title="Liébana">Liébana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Campoo" title="Campoo">Campoo-Los Valles</a>, rural and industrial by regions.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Natural regions</b> (regarding geographical features)
<ul><li>Coastal strip</li>
<li>Central strip (Cantabrian valleys perpendicular to the coast): Liébana, Saja and Nansa, Besaya, Pas and Miera (or Valles Pasiegos), and Asón-Gándara valleys.</li>
<li>Southern strip (Rivers Ebro and Duero's basins): Campoo and Southern valleys</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Historic regions</b></li></ul>
<p>Until the 13th century, Cantabria was organized in valleys, as was typical in all of northern Spain. From then on, it was substituted by the organization in cities, towns or historic <i>comarcas</i> that grouped several valleys.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg/200px-Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg/300px-Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg/400px-Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2548" data-file-height="1911" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santander.Banco.Santander.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Banco_Santander" title="Banco Santander">Banco Santander</a> headquarters, in <i>Paseo de Pereda</i>, Santander</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a> of Cantabria has <a href="/wiki/Primary_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary industry">primary industry</a>, now in decline, employing 5.8% of the active population in the sectors of cattle farming, traditional dairy farming, and meat production; agriculture, especially corn, potatoes, vegetables, and roughage; maritime fishing; and the mining of <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarries</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Secondary_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Secondary industry">secondary industry</a> which employs 30.3% of the active population is the sector with the most productivity in recent years due to construction; that of <a href="/wiki/Ironwork" title="Ironwork">ironworking</a> (being Reinosa the most important city), food service (milk, meat, vegetables and seafood), <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemistry</a> (Solvay, Sniace), paper production (Sinace, Papelera del Besaya), <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textile</a> fabrication (Textil Santanderina in Cabezón de la Sal), <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a> (Moehs in Requejada), industrial groups and transport, etc. The <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> employs 63.8% of the active population and is increasing, given that large concentrations of the population live in the urban centers and the importance that <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> has acquired in the recent years. As of July 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> rate in Cantabria is 19.3%, compared to 24.47% in Spain; while as of April 2010 its <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> was €25,326, compared to €26,100 in Spain and €25,100 in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>25. In 2007, Cantabria's growth of real <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> was 4.1%, compared to a 3.9% average for Spain.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_and_communications">Transportation and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transportation and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santander.Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Santander.Airport.jpg/200px-Santander.Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Santander.Airport.jpg/300px-Santander.Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Santander.Airport.jpg/400px-Santander.Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2728" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santander.Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parayas airport, located in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Camargo,_Cantabria" title="Camargo, Cantabria">Camargo</a>, 5 km from Santander</div></div></div>
<p>The most significant consequence of the strong relief of the Cantabrian territory is the existence of topographic barriers that condition decisively the courses of the linking infrastructures, as much in the north-south orientation in the accesses to the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Spain#The_Inner_Plateau_and_associated_mountains" title="Geography of Spain">Castilian Mesa</a>, as in the east-west in the communication between valleys. Moreover, the cost of their construction and maintenance is much higher than average.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The main communications infrastructures of the region are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Santander_Airport" title="Santander Airport">Santander Airport</a></li>
<li>Cantabrian Motorway (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-8" title="Autovía A-8">Autovía A-8</a>, European route E-70)</li>
<li>Cantabria-Meseta Motorway (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-67" title="Autovía A-67">Autovía A-67</a>)</li>
<li>Narrow-gauge <a href="/wiki/Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway">railway</a> <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a>-<a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> (<a href="/wiki/FEVE" class="mw-redirect" title="FEVE">FEVE</a>)</li>
<li>Narrow-gauge railway Santander-<a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> (FEVE)</li>
<li>Broad-gauge railway Santander-<a href="/wiki/Palencia" title="Palencia">Palencia</a>-<a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>-<a href="/wiki/%C3%81vila,_Spain" title="Ávila, Spain">Ávila</a>-<a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> (<a href="/wiki/RENFE" class="mw-redirect" title="RENFE">RENFE</a>)</li>
<li>Broad-gauge high-speed railway Santander-<a href="/wiki/Torrelavega" title="Torrelavega">Torrelavega</a>-<a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>-<a href="/wiki/Segovia" title="Segovia">Segovia</a>-<a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> (<a href="/wiki/RENFE" class="mw-redirect" title="RENFE">RENFE</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">Ferry</a> line Santander-<a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_media_and_public_opinion">Mass media and public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mass media and public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In Cantabria, there are two daily regional newspapers in addition to the national ones: <i>El Diario Montañés</i> and <i>Alerta</i>, as well as many weekly, fortnightly and monthly publications. The main national radio stations have transmitter stations in places like Santander, Torrelavega, Castro-Urdiales, or Reinosa. There are also numerous local and regional stations. For the moment, there is no Cantabrian autonomic television with public financing, although some local channels exist (including Canal 8 DM, TeleBahía, Telecabarga, Localia TV Cantabria, etc.). In recent years, the Internet has allowed new informative proposals to emerge in the shape of digital diaries or blogs, which contribute to enrich the mediatic panorama of the region.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Techo_de_Altamira_(replica)-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Techo_de_Altamira_%28replica%29-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg/200px-Techo_de_Altamira_%28replica%29-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Techo_de_Altamira_%28replica%29-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg/300px-Techo_de_Altamira_%28replica%29-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Techo_de_Altamira_%28replica%29-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg/400px-Techo_de_Altamira_%28replica%29-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Techo_de_Altamira_(replica)-Museo_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_Nacional.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Altamira_Cave" class="mw-redirect" title="Altamira Cave">Altamira Cave</a> paintings, made by <a href="/wiki/Cro-Magnon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cro-Magnon">Cro-Magnons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline.co.uk_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline.co.uk-35">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the official language of Cantabria. The eastern part of Cantabria contributed to the origins of Castilian Spanish in a significant way. In the western part there are remnants of the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_dialect" title="Cantabrian dialect">Cantabrian language</a>, or "mountain language", and it is also somewhat preserved in parts of the Pas and Soba valleys in its eastern zone. This language has neither regulation nor official recognition in Cantabria.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monuments_and_museums">Monuments and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Monuments and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png/100px-La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png/150px-La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png/200px-La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png 2x" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Pasiega-Galeria_C-panel_77.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the many paleolithic paintings in the <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_La_Pasiega" title="Cave of La Pasiega">Cave of La Pasiega</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><b>Caves</b>: <a href="/wiki/Altamira_(cave)" class="mw-redirect" title="Altamira (cave)">Altamira Cave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_El_Soplao" title="Cave of El Soplao">El Soplao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cave_del_Valle_(Cantabria)" title="Cave del Valle (Cantabria)">Del Valle</a>, El Pendo, <a href="/wiki/Cueva_de_La_Pasiega" class="mw-redirect" title="Cueva de La Pasiega">La Pasiega Cave</a>, Las Monedas, El Castillo, Morín, and others.</li>
<li><b>Civil architecture</b>: <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_la_Magdalena" title="Palacio de la Magdalena">Magdalena palace</a> in Santander; Capricho de Gaudí, <a href="/wiki/Comillas_Pontifical_University" title="Comillas Pontifical University">Pontifical University of Comillas</a> and Sobrellano palace in Comillas; Bárcena palace in Ampuero; Castle of Argüeso in Campoo; Hornillos palace in Las Fraguas del Besaya; etc.</li>
<li><b>Religious architecture</b>: Collegiate of Santillana del Mar, Collegiate of Santa Cruz de Castañeda, <a href="/wiki/Santo_Toribio_de_Li%C3%A9bana" title="Santo Toribio de Liébana">Santo Toribio de Liébana Monastery</a>, Santa María de Lebeña, Santa María de Piasca, Santa María del Puerto, San Román del Moroso, Santa Catalina del Cintul, Santuario de Virgen de la Peña, ermita de San Cipriano, ermita de Monte Corona, etc.</li>
<li><b>Museums</b>: Cantabrian Sea Maritime Museum, Ethnographic Museum of Cantabria, Santander Museum of Fine Arts, Regional Museum of Prehistory and Arqueology of Cantabria, Cantabrian Museum of Nature, Altamira National Museum and Investigation Centre, and others.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg/200px-Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg/300px-Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg/400px-Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1571" data-file-height="1135" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_la_Magdalena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>International University Menéndez Pelayo</b>. <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_la_Magdalena" title="Palacio de la Magdalena">Palacio de la Magdalena</a>. Venue for the summer courses of the UIMP (Santander). It also was a seasonal residence for kings of Spain.</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Cantabria" title="University of Cantabria">University of Cantabria</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_University_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo" class="mw-redirect" title="International University Menéndez Pelayo">International University Menéndez Pelayo</a></li>

<li>Campus Comillas</li>
<li>CESINE</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fairs_and_festivals">Fairs and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fairs and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Vijanera.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/La_Vijanera.jpg/200px-La_Vijanera.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/La_Vijanera.jpg/300px-La_Vijanera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/La_Vijanera.jpg/400px-La_Vijanera.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Vijanera.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/La_Vijanera" title="La Vijanera">La Vijanera</a> in Silió</div></div></div>
<p>Regarding the <a href="/wiki/Fair" title="Fair">fairs</a>, understood as big markets of products periodically celebrated, it is remarkable the <i>Livestock Fair of Torrelavega</i> taking place in the National Livestock Market "Jesús Collado Soto", the third biggest of Spain, that groups the buy and sell of all kinds of cattle in the region itself and the adjacent ones, being the bovine the main product. All over the region cattle and typical products fairs are celebrated weekly, monthly, or annually to gather the neighbours of the land. There are many different festivities in Cantabria, some of them limited just to small villages, but there are also festivals that attract tourism from all over the country. The most important are the following:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/La_Vijanera" title="La Vijanera">La Vijanera</a></i> (Winter Carnival), celebrated during the first Sunday of the year in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sili%C3%B3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Silió (page does not exist)">Silió</a>. It celebrates the end of the short winter days and the arrival of the sun. The representation of a white bear hunt takes place all over this little village. The traditional dressing of the characters in the play, the trapajones and the zarramacos, is one of its main features.</li>
<li><i>Carnaval marinero</i> (Sailor Carnival), in February in <a href="/wiki/Santo%C3%B1a" title="Santoña">Santoña</a>. Commonly known as "the carnivals of the North", in this carnival, started in 1934, many people of the town participate dressing themselves up as fish. The main event is the "Trial at the bottom of the ocean", where the "<i><a href="/wiki/Bream" title="Bream">besugo</a></i>" is judged before the last act, "The burning of the <i>besugo</i>". (A <i>besugo</i> is a foolish person besides a type of fish).</li>
<li><i>La Folía</i>, April in <a href="/wiki/San_Vicente_de_la_Barquera" title="San Vicente de la Barquera">San Vicente de la Barquera</a>, a parade of local fishing boats following one with a statue of the Virgin.</li>
<li><i>Coso Blanco</i>, first Friday in July in Castro Urdiales. Colorful parade with carts.</li>
<li><i>Cantabria Day</i>, second Sunday of August in <a href="/wiki/Cabez%C3%B3n_de_la_Sal" title="Cabezón de la Sal">Cabezón de la Sal</a>. Traditional Cantabrian music, ceramics fair, local foods, <a href="/wiki/Bolo_palma" title="Bolo palma">bolo palma</a> championships, ox dragging contests and public speeches.</li>
<li>SAUGA folk music festival, celebrated the third weekend of August in <a href="/wiki/Colindres" title="Colindres">Colindres</a>.</li>
<li><i>Floral Gala</i>, August en <a href="/wiki/Torrelavega" title="Torrelavega">Torrelavega</a>. A festival of international touristic importance with carts decorated with flowers.</li>
<li><i>Battle of Flowers</i>, August, in Laredo. Carts decorated with flowers and fruit. <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">Fireworks</a> in the evening.</li>
<li><i>Campoo Day</i>, September in <a href="/wiki/Reinosa" title="Reinosa">Reinosa</a>. Tourist fair of regional importance since 1977 and celebrated since the 19th century, it shows customs and traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Campoo" title="Campoo">Campurrians</a> in their capital. <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">Cattle</a> shows, local products market and regional costumes are the items in this festival.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<p>The following <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">festivals</a> are also remarkable in modern Cantabrian culture: <a href="/wiki/Santander_International_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander International Festival">Santander International Festival</a><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> (Arts festival), Santander Summer Festival<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> (Music festival), Sotocine<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> (Film festival)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mythology">Mythology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mythology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_mythology" title="Cantabrian mythology">Cantabrian mythology</a></div>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The north of the Spanish state is a rich area for <a href="/wiki/Mythology" class="mw-redirect" title="Mythology">mythology</a>. From <a href="/wiki/Galicia,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Galicia, Spain">Galicia</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, passing by Asturias and Cantabria, there are rites, stories and imaginary or impossible beings (or maybe not so).
</p><p>Cantabrian lore turns its forests and mountains into magical places where the <a href="/wiki/Myth" title="Myth">myths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belief" title="Belief">beliefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legend" title="Legend">legends</a> have been present as an essential part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabrian_culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cantabrian culture (page does not exist)">Cantabrian culture</a>, either because they have been living in the popular heritage through the <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral tradition</a> transmitted from father to son, or because they have been recovered by scholars (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Manuel_Llano&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Manuel Llano (page does not exist)">Manuel Llano</a> and others) who have worried about preserving the cultural heritage.
Its mythology and <a href="/wiki/Superstition" title="Superstition">superstitions</a> present a great <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic</a> influence that has diluted with the pass of time, being <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome" title="Religion in ancient Rome">romanized</a> or <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianized</a> in many cases.
</p><p>There is a heavy presence of fabulous beings of <a href="/wiki/Giant_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant (mythology)">giant</a> proportions and <a href="/wiki/Cyclopean" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclopean">Cyclopean</a> features (the <i><a href="/wiki/Oj%C3%A1ncanu" title="Ojáncanu">ojáncanos</a></i>), fantastic animals (<i><a href="/wiki/Cu%C3%A9lebre" title="Cuélebre">culebres</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Caballucos_del_diablu" class="mw-redirect" title="Caballucos del diablu">caballucos del diablu</a></i> (lit. horses of the devil, <a href="/wiki/Damselfly" title="Damselfly">damselflies</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Ramidreju" title="Ramidreju">ramidrejus</a></i>, etc.), <a href="/wiki/Fairy" title="Fairy">færies</a> (<i>anjanas</i>, <i>ijanas</i> of Aras), <a href="/wiki/Duende_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Duende (mythology)">duendes</a> (<i>nuberos, ventolines, <a href="/wiki/Trenti" title="Trenti">trentis</a>, trasgus, trastolillos, musgosu, tentiruju</i>), <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropomorphic">anthropomorphic</a> characters (the <i>sirenuca</i> (little mermaid), the <a href="/wiki/Fish-man" title="Fish-man">fish-man</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cuegle" title="Cuegle">cuegle</a>, the wife-bear of Andara, the <i>guajona</i>), etc.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_cuisine" title="Cantabrian cuisine">Cantabrian cuisine</a></div>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li><b>Typical dishes</b>: <i><a href="/wiki/Cocido_monta%C3%B1%C3%A9s" title="Cocido montañés">Cocido montañés</a></i> (<i>Highlander stew</i>) made with <a href="/wiki/Common_bean" class="mw-redirect" title="Common bean">beans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collard_greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Collard greens">collard greens</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Cocido_lebaniego" title="Cocido lebaniego">cocido lebaniego</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A9bana" title="Liébana">Liébanan</a> stew</i>) made from <a href="/wiki/Chickpea" title="Chickpea">chickpeas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marmita" class="mw-redirect" title="Marmita">marmita</a>).</li>
<li><b>Meat dishes</b>: <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">Beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ox" title="Ox">ox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a> or <a href="/wiki/Boar" class="mw-redirect" title="Boar">boar</a>. Cooked on the grill, stewed or with vegetables.</li></ul>
<dl><dd>The livestock farming reputation of the region and its climatological conditions favouring <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a> breeding allowed the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> to pass the "Meats of Cantabria" denomination as a <i><a href="/wiki/Protected_geographical_indications_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected geographical indications in the European Union">Protected Geographic Denomination</a></i> for the beef of certain kinds of native races (<i>Tudanca</i>, <i>Monchina</i>) and others adapted to the environment or integrated by assimilation (<i>Brown Alpine</i>).</dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>Fish and seafood</b>: <a href="/wiki/Anchovy" title="Anchovy">Anchovies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lophius_piscatorius" title="Lophius piscatorius">angler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hake" title="Hake">hake</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_seabass" class="mw-redirect" title="European seabass">sea bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soleidae" title="Soleidae">sole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_horse_mackerel" title="Atlantic horse mackerel">mackerel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sardine" title="Sardine">sardine</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_anchovy" title="European anchovy">European anchovies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonito" title="Bonito">bonito</a> of the North (of Spain), <a href="/wiki/Gilt-head_bream" title="Gilt-head bream">gilt-head bream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_bream" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea bream">sea bream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_mullet" title="Red mullet">red mullet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scorpaenidae" title="Scorpaenidae">scorpionfish</a>, as well as some river fish such as <a href="/wiki/Trout" title="Trout">trout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a>. <i>Rabas</i> (fried <a href="/wiki/Calamari" class="mw-redirect" title="Calamari">calamari</a>) and <i>cachón en su tinta</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cuttlefish" title="Cuttlefish">cuttlefish</a> cooked in its own ink) are local specialties. <a href="/wiki/Clam" title="Clam">Clam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_mussel" title="Blue mussel">mussel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ensis" title="Ensis">muergos (jackknife)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cockle_(bivalve)" title="Cockle (bivalve)">cockle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velvet_crab" title="Velvet crab">velvet crab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maja_squinado" title="Maja squinado">spider crab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pollicipes_pollicipes" title="Pollicipes pollicipes">goose barnacle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_periwinkle" title="Common periwinkle">periwinkle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway_lobster" class="mw-redirect" title="Norway lobster">Norway lobster</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_lobster" class="mw-redirect" title="European lobster">European lobster</a> are available.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><b>Desserts</b>: <i><a href="/wiki/Quesada_Pasiega" class="mw-redirect" title="Quesada Pasiega">Quesadas</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sobao" title="Sobao">sobaos</a></i> of the Pas valley; <a href="/wiki/Unquera" title="Unquera">Unquera</a>'s Corbatas and <a href="/wiki/Torrelavega" title="Torrelavega">Torrelavega</a>'s polkas both basically <a href="/wiki/Puff_pastry" title="Puff pastry">puff pastry</a>); Palucos de Cabezón de la Sal; and Pantortillas of Reinosa.</li>
<li><b>Cheeses</b>: Quesucos de Liébana.</li>
<li><b>Drinks</b>: <a href="/wiki/Txakoli" title="Txakoli">Chacolí</a>; <a href="/wiki/Apple_cider" title="Apple cider">apple cider</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orujo" title="Orujo">orujo</a> (liquor made from <a href="/wiki/Pomace" title="Pomace">pomace</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A9bana" title="Liébana">Liébana</a>; and tostadillo from <a href="/wiki/Potes" title="Potes">Potes</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG/200px-Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG/300px-Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG/400px-Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regata_Pedre%C3%B1a.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Trainera</i> regatta at the <a href="/wiki/Santander_bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander bay">Santander bay</a></div></div></div>
<p>The traditional sport of Cantabria is the game of <i>bolos</i><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Skittles_(sport)" title="Skittles (sport)">skittles</a>) in its four forms: <i><a href="/wiki/Bolo_palma" title="Bolo palma">bolo palma</a></i>, <i>pasabolo tablón</i>, <i>pasabolo losa</i> and <i>bolo pasiego</i>. The first one is the most widespread, exceeding regional nature and reaching the eastern zone of Asturias and also being the most complex in its game rules. The existence of <i>boleras</i> or skittle rings is important in every Cantabrian township, often being near the church or the village pub. Since the late 1980s, skittle play has consolidated with the reinforcement of skittle schools, revamped by different town councils and Cantabrian institutions, various competitions, and media coverage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The remo (<a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>) is a very traditional sport in the coastal towns. The origins of rowing in Cantabria go back many centuries, when several <i><a href="/wiki/Trainera" title="Trainera">traineras</a></i> (traditional fishing <a href="/wiki/Longboat" title="Longboat">longboats</a>) competed for the selling of the caught fish, which was reserved for the first ship to arrive to the <a href="/wiki/Fish_market" title="Fish market">fish market</a>. At the end of the 19th century, work became sport and people started to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Regatta" title="Regatta">regattas</a> between Cantabrian townships. The sport clubs of Cantabria, especially the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sociedad_Deportiva_de_Remo_Astillero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sociedad Deportiva de Remo Astillero (page does not exist)">Astillero</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sociedad_Deportiva_de_Remo_Castro_Urdiales&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sociedad Deportiva de Remo Castro Urdiales (page does not exist)">Castro Urdiales</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sociedad_Deportiva_de_Remo_Pedre%C3%B1a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sociedad Deportiva de Remo Pedreña (page does not exist)">Pedreña</a> belong to the most prize-winning teams of the history of this sport, and nowadays they are having one of the best moments after a decades-long period of trophy drought.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg/300px-Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg/450px-Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg/600px-Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1456" data-file-height="471" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_los_Deportes_de_Santander.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Santander Sports Palace: a basketball game featuring the local team, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cantabria_Lobos" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantabria Lobos">Cantabria Lobos</a></i> (wolves).</div></div></div>
<p>The Pasiegan jump is another of the outstanding rural sports of the region and a clear example of how the use of a work skill that disappears with the pass of time, gives rise to games and competition. Similar to other forms, like the <a href="/wiki/Salto_del_pastor" title="Salto del pastor">Canarian shepherd jump</a>, in the beginning this technique was used in the Pasiegan valleys to cross the stone walls, the fences, the creeks or the ravines that bordered the fields and obstructed the pass in the abrupt geography of the highland areas of Cantabria.
</p><p>Referring to mass sports, Cantabria is present in national and international competitions through teams such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Racing_de_Santander" title="Racing de Santander">Racing de Santander</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/RS_Gimn%C3%A1stica_de_Torrelavega" class="mw-redirect" title="RS Gimnástica de Torrelavega">RS Gimnástica de Torrelavega</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Cantabria_autonomous_football_team" title="Cantabria autonomous football team">Cantabria autonomous football team</a> in <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Spain" title="Football in Spain">football</a>  or the <i><a href="/wiki/Independiente_RC" title="Independiente RC">Independiente RC</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Divisi%C3%B3n_de_Honor_de_Rugby" title="División de Honor de Rugby">rugby union</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/CB_Cantabria" title="CB Cantabria">Club Balonmano Cantabria</a></i> that won <a href="/wiki/Liga_ASOBAL" title="Liga ASOBAL">Leagues</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey_de_Balonmano" title="Copa del Rey de Balonmano">King's Cups</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/IHF_Super_Globe" title="IHF Super Globe">IHF Super Globe</a>, <a href="/wiki/EHF_Champions_League" title="EHF Champions League">EHF Champions League</a>, <a href="/wiki/EHF_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="EHF Cup Winners&#39; Cup">EHF Cup Winners' Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/EHF_Cup" title="EHF Cup">EHF Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Cantabria_Baloncesto" title="Cantabria Baloncesto">Cantabria Lobos</a> that played in the <a href="/wiki/Liga_ACB" title="Liga ACB">ACB</a> in <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> represented the highest level of the Cantabrian sport in the recent past.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Cantabrians">Notable Cantabrians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cantabria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notable Cantabrians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo,_por_Kaulak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo%2C_por_Kaulak.jpg/200px-Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo%2C_por_Kaulak.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo%2C_por_Kaulak.jpg/300px-Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo%2C_por_Kaulak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo%2C_por_Kaulak.jpg/400px-Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo%2C_por_Kaulak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="644" data-file-height="811" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo,_por_Kaulak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marcelino_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcelino Menéndez Pelayo">Marcelino Menéndez Pelayo</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Cantabrian_people" title="Category:Cantabrian people">Category:Cantabrian people</a></div>
<p>Cantabria has been the birthplace of exceptional and notable individuals in fields such as literature, arts, sciences, etc. Many of them have played a decisive role, not only in the history and events of the region, but also on the national and international levels. These include:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Business</b>: <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_de_Polanco" title="Jesús de Polanco">Jesús de Polanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Bot%C3%ADn" title="Emilio Botín">Emilio Botín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ana_Patricia_Bot%C3%ADn" class="mw-redirect" title="Ana Patricia Botín">Ana Patricia Botin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Vicente Calderón">Vicente Calderon</a></li>
<li><b>Sports</b>: <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Gento" title="Francisco Gento">Francisco Gento</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santillana_(footballer)" title="Santillana (footballer)">"Santillana"</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Abascal" title="José Manuel Abascal">José Manuel Abascal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seve_Ballesteros" title="Seve Ballesteros">Seve Ballesteros</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Freire" title="Óscar Freire">Óscar Freire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Cobo" title="Juan José Cobo">Juan José Cobo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cecilio_Lastra" title="Cecilio Lastra">Cecilio Lastra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Ventoso" title="Francisco Ventoso">Francisco Ventoso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Beitia" title="Ruth Beitia">Ruth Beitia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Canales" title="Sergio Canales">Sergio Canales</a></li>
<li><b>Music</b>: <a href="/wiki/Ata%C3%BAlfo_Argenta" title="Ataúlfo Argenta">Ataúlfo Argenta</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bustamante" title="David Bustamante">David Bustamante</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Fuga_(band)" title="La Fuga (band)">La Fuga</a></li>
<li><b>Film, radio, and TV</b>: <a href="/wiki/Mario_Camus" title="Mario Camus">Mario Camus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Guti%C3%A9rrez_Arag%C3%B3n" title="Manuel Gutiérrez Aragón">Manuel Gutiérrez Aragón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Noriega_(Spanish_actor)" title="Eduardo Noriega (Spanish actor)">Eduardo Noriega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Resines" title="Antonio Resines">Antonio Resines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nacho_Vigalondo" title="Nacho Vigalondo">Nacho Vigalondo</a>.</li>
<li><b>Military</b>: <a href="/wiki/Corocotta" title="Corocotta">Corocotta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Velarde" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro Velarde">Pedro Velarde</a></li>
<li><b>Religion</b>: <a href="/wiki/Emeterius_and_Celedonius" title="Emeterius and Celedonius">San Emeterio, San Celedonio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beatus_of_Li%C3%A9bana" title="Beatus of Liébana">Beatus of Liébana</a></li>
<li><b>Explorers</b>: <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cosa" title="Juan de la Cosa">Juan de la Cosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vital_Alsar" title="Vital Alsar">Vital Alsar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Bustamante_y_Guerra" title="José de Bustamante y Guerra">José de Bustamante y Guerra</a></li>
<li><b>Literature</b>: <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Calder%C3%B3n_de_la_Barca" title="Pedro Calderón de la Barca">Pedro Calderon de la Barca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lope_de_Vega" title="Lope de Vega">Lope de Vega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Pereda" title="José María de Pereda">José María de Pereda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concha_Espina" title="Concha Espina">Concha Espina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerardo_Diego" title="Gerardo Diego">Gerardo Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Pombo" title="Álvaro Pombo">Álvaro Pombo</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Luys_Santa_Marina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Luys Santa Marina (page does not exist)">Luys Santa Marina</a>.</li>
<li><b>Painting</b>: <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Blanchard" title="María Blanchard">María Blanchard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Madrazo" class="mw-redirect" title="José de Madrazo">José de Madrazo</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Gonz%C3%A1lez_G%C3%B3mez" title="Francisco González Gómez">Francisco González Gómez</a></li>
<li><b>Science and technology</b>: <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Torres_Quevedo" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonardo Torres Quevedo">Leonardo Torres Quevedo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Herrera" title="Juan de Herrera">Juan de Herrera</a></li>
<li><b>Politics</b>: <a href="/wiki/Luis_Carrero_Blanco" title="Luis Carrero Blanco">Luis Carrero Blanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Zamanillo_Gonz%C3%A1lez-Camino" title="José Luis Zamanillo González-Camino">José Luis Zamanillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_P%C3%A9rez_Rubalcaba" title="Alfredo Pérez Rubalcaba">Alfredo Pérez Rubalcaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Leguina" title="Joaquín Leguina">Joaquín Leguina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Revilla" title="Miguel Ángel Revilla">Miguel Ángel Revilla</a></li>
<li><b>Sociology</b>: <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Cobo_Bed%C3%ADa" title="Rosa Cobo Bedía">Rosa Cobo Bedía</a></li></ul>

Updated by Portal de la Constitución. 2005. Updated 2007; retrieved 9 June 2007.</span>
</li>
